AITRAS shall evaluate the quality, location, and context of the Order Block before considering it as supporting evidence.

13.4.2 Purpose

Order Block Alignment helps AITRAS to:

Validate institutional interest.

Strengthen the Market Thesis.

Improve trade location.

Filter weak or invalid Order Blocks.

Increase confidence in high-quality setups.

13.4.3 Core Principles

Only validated Order Blocks shall be considered.

Higher-timeframe Order Blocks carry greater significance.

Fresh Order Blocks are generally stronger than mitigated ones.

Order Blocks should align with Market Structure and Liquidity.

An Order Block is supporting evidence, not a standalone trading signal.

13.4.4 AI Investigation Checklist

AITRAS shall determine:

Is the Order Block valid?

Is it Bullish or Bearish?

Is it Fresh or Mitigated?

Does it align with the Higher-Timeframe Bias?

Does it align with Market Structure?

Is it supported by Liquidity and FVGs?

Does it strengthen or weaken the Market Thesis?

13.4.5 Alignment Classification

AITRAS shall classify Order Block Alignment as:

Alignment

Description

Strong Alignment

A validated Order Block clearly supports the proposed trade direction.

Moderate Alignment

The Order Block generally supports the Market Thesis but has minor weaknesses.

Weak Alignment

The Order Block provides limited supporting evidence.

Conflicting Alignment

The Order Block contradicts the proposed Market Thesis or has been invalidated.

13.4.6 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Increase confidence when a high-quality Order Block supports the analysis.

Reduce confidence if the Order Block is weak or mitigated.

Reject the Order Block as evidence if it has been invalidated.

Explain how the Order Block influenced the overall Market Thesis.

13.4.7 Summary

Key Principles

Only validated Order Blocks contribute to confluence.

Higher-timeframe and fresh Order Blocks have greater influence.

Order Blocks must align with Market Structure and Liquidity.

Weak or invalid Order Blocks reduce confidence.

Order Block Alignment contributes to the overall Confidence Score.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall evaluate whether a validated Order Block supports the proposed Market Thesis. The AI shall increase or decrease the Confidence Score based on the quality, timeframe, freshness, and alignment of the Order Block with Market Structure, Liquidity, and the Higher-Timeframe Bias. An Order Block alone shall never justify a trading decision.

Contribution to Confluence Score

Order Block Alignment should influence the overall Confidence Score as follows:

Strong Alignment: High positive contribution.

Moderate Alignment: Moderate positive contribution.

Weak Alignment: Small positive or neutral contribution.

Conflicting Alignment: Negative contribution that may require the Market Thesis to be reviewed.

Chapter Status

13.4 — Order Block Alignment: Complete.

Confluence Engine Progress

The AI is now evaluating:

✅ Trend Alignment

✅ Liquidity Alignment

✅ Structure Alignment

✅ Order Block Alignment

These four components form the core institutional framework that AITRAS will use to build and validate its Market Thesis before moving on to additional evidence such as Fair Value Gaps, Sessions, News, Risk, and the final Confidence Score.

13.5 Fair Value Gap (FVG) Alignment

Evaluating Whether Fair Value Gaps Support the Market Thesis

13.5.1 Definition

Fair Value Gap (FVG) Alignment is the process of determining whether a validated Fair Value Gap supports, weakens, or contradicts the proposed Market Thesis.

AITRAS shall evaluate the location, quality, and context of the FVG before considering it as supporting evidence.

13.5.2 Purpose

FVG Alignment helps AITRAS to:

Confirm institutional price imbalance.

Improve trade location.

Strengthen the Market Thesis.

Filter low-quality or irrelevant FVGs.

Increase confidence in high-probability setups.

13.5.3 Core Principles

Only validated FVGs shall be considered.

Higher-timeframe FVGs carry greater significance.

Fresh, unmitigated FVGs are generally stronger than fully mitigated ones.

FVGs should align with Market Structure, Liquidity, and Higher-Timeframe Bias.

An FVG is supporting evidence, not a standalone trading signal.

13.5.4 AI Investigation Checklist

AITRAS shall determine:

Is the FVG valid?

Is it Bullish or Bearish?

Has it been mitigated?

Does it align with the Higher-Timeframe Bias?

Does it align with Market Structure?

Is there supporting Liquidity?

Is there a related Order Block?

Does the FVG strengthen or weaken the Market Thesis?

13.5.5 Alignment Classification

AITRAS shall classify FVG Alignment as:

Alignment

Description

Strong Alignment

A validated FVG clearly supports the proposed trade direction.

Moderate Alignment

The FVG generally supports the Market Thesis but has minor weaknesses.

Weak Alignment

The FVG provides limited supporting evidence.

Conflicting Alignment

The FVG contradicts the proposed Market Thesis or has lost its significance.

13.5.6 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Increase confidence when a high-quality FVG supports the Market Thesis.

Reduce confidence when the FVG has already been mitigated or lacks supporting evidence.

Reject the FVG as meaningful evidence if it conflicts with higher-timeframe analysis.

Explain how the FVG influenced the final recommendation.

13.5.7 Summary

Key Principles

Only validated FVGs contribute to confluence.

Higher-timeframe FVGs carry greater weight.

Fresh, unmitigated FVGs provide stronger evidence.

FVGs should support Market Structure and Liquidity.

FVG Alignment contributes to the overall Confidence Score.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall evaluate whether a validated Fair Value Gap supports the proposed Market Thesis. The AI shall adjust the Confidence Score based on the quality, timeframe, mitigation status, and alignment of the FVG with Market Structure, Liquidity, Order Blocks, and the Higher-Timeframe Bias. A Fair Value Gap shall never be treated as sufficient evidence on its own.

Contribution to Confluence Score

FVG Alignment should influence the overall Confidence Score as follows:

Strong Alignment: High positive contribution.

Moderate Alignment: Moderate positive contribution.

Weak Alignment: Small positive or neutral contribution.

Conflicting Alignment: Negative contribution that weakens the Market Thesis.

Chapter Status

13.5 — Fair Value Gap (FVG) Alignment: Complete.

Design Recommendation

As we continue building AITRAS, I suggest we distinguish between core evidence and supporting evidence within the Confluence Engine.

Core Evidence (highest priority):

Trend Alignment

Structure Alignment

Liquidity Alignment

Supporting Evidence (adds confidence):

Order Block Alignment

FVG Alignment

Session Alignment

News Alignment

Risk Alignment

This reflects how professional market analysis is typically performed: the market's direction is established first, and then supporting concepts are used to confirm or weaken the thesis. It also provides a clearer framework for calculating the final Confidence Score in a consistent and explainable way.

13.6 Session Alignment

Evaluating Whether the Current Trading Session Supports the Market Thesis

13.6.1 Definition

Session Alignment is the process of determining whether the current Forex trading session provides favorable conditions for the proposed Market Thesis.

AITRAS shall evaluate market activity, liquidity, volatility, and session characteristics to determine whether the timing supports trade execution.

13.6.2 Purpose

Session Alignment helps AITRAS to:

Confirm that the market is active enough for the setup.

Avoid low-probability trades during quiet periods.

Improve execution timing.

Increase confidence when expected session behavior supports the analysis.

Reduce confidence when session conditions contradict the Market Thesis.

13.6.3 Core Principles

Different trading sessions exhibit different market behaviors.

High liquidity generally produces more reliable price movements.

Major institutional activity occurs during the London and New York sessions.

Session overlaps often provide increased volatility and trading opportunities.

Session timing should support, not replace, technical analysis.

13.6.4 AI Investigation Checklist

AITRAS shall determine:

What trading session is currently active?

Is the market in a major session or a low-liquidity period?

Is there a London–New York session overlap?

Does the current session typically support the expected market movement?

Is volatility appropriate for the proposed trade?

Does the session strengthen or weaken the Market Thesis?

13.6.5 Alignment Classification

AITRAS shall classify Session Alignment as:

Alignment

Description

Strong Alignment

Current session strongly supports the expected move with favorable liquidity and volatility.

Moderate Alignment

Session generally supports the trade but with reduced activity or momentum.

Weak Alignment

Session provides limited support due to lower liquidity or reduced volatility.

Conflicting Alignment

Current session is unsuitable for the proposed trade and may reduce its probability of success.

13.6.6 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Increase confidence when the active session supports the Market Thesis.

Reduce confidence during periods of low liquidity or abnormal market conditions.

Consider delaying execution if a higher-quality session is approaching.

Explain how the current trading session influenced the recommendation.

13.6.7 Summary

Key Principles

Market timing influences trade quality.

High-liquidity sessions provide stronger confirmation.

Session overlaps often increase trading opportunities.

Low-liquidity periods require greater caution.

Session Alignment contributes to the overall Confidence Score.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall evaluate the current trading session before recommending execution. The AI shall determine whether session-specific liquidity, volatility, and institutional participation support the proposed Market Thesis. Session Alignment shall strengthen or weaken the overall Confidence Score but shall never override higher-priority evidence such as Market Structure or Liquidity.

Contribution to Confluence Score

Session Alignment should influence the overall Confidence Score as follows:

Strong Alignment: Moderate positive contribution.

Moderate Alignment: Small positive contribution.

Weak Alignment: Neutral or slight negative contribution.

Conflicting Alignment: Negative contribution that may justify delaying execution.

Chapter Status

13.6 — Session Alignment: Complete.

AITRAS Priority Reminder

At this point, the Confluence Engine should evaluate evidence in a consistent hierarchy:

Trend Alignment

Structure Alignment

Liquidity Alignment

Order Block Alignment

Fair Value Gap (FVG) Alignment

Session Alignment

Each alignment contributes independently to the overall Confidence Score, ensuring that no single factor determines the final recommendation. This makes AITRAS' reasoning transparent, explainable, and robust.

13.7 News Alignment

Evaluating Whether Fundamental Events Support the Market Thesis

13.7.1 Definition

News Alignment is the process of determining whether current or upcoming economic events support, weaken, or contradict the proposed Market Thesis.

AITRAS shall analyze scheduled economic releases, central bank events, and major geopolitical developments before recommending a trade.

13.7.2 Purpose

News Alignment helps AITRAS to:

Identify potential market-moving events.

Avoid entering trades during excessive uncertainty.

Confirm whether fundamentals support technical analysis.

Reduce the risk of unexpected volatility.

Improve the reliability of trade recommendations.

13.7.3 Core Principles

High-impact news can rapidly change market direction.

Technical analysis should be evaluated alongside fundamental events.

Scheduled news must be reviewed before trade execution.

News should be considered in terms of its likely market impact, not just its existence.

Market reaction is more important than the headline alone.

13.7.4 AI Investigation Checklist

AITRAS shall determine:

Are there any upcoming high-impact economic events?

Which currencies or instruments are affected?

How much time remains before the event?

Does the expected outcome support the Market Thesis?

Has recent news already changed market sentiment?

Is it safer to wait until after the news release?

13.7.5 Alignment Classification

AITRAS shall classify News Alignment as:

Alignment

Description

Strong Alignment

Current fundamentals support the Market Thesis and no major conflicting news is expected.

Moderate Alignment

Minor news events exist but are unlikely to significantly affect the setup.

Weak Alignment

News introduces uncertainty that reduces confidence.

Conflicting Alignment

High-impact news contradicts the Market Thesis or creates unacceptable uncertainty.

13.7.6 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Increase confidence when fundamental conditions support the Market Thesis.

Reduce confidence when important news introduces uncertainty.

Recommend waiting when a high-impact event is imminent and may invalidate the setup.

Reassess the Market Thesis immediately after significant news releases.

Clearly explain how news influenced the final recommendation.

13.7.7 Summary

Key Principles

High-impact news can strengthen or invalidate technical setups.

Scheduled economic events must be reviewed before execution.

Market reaction is more important than forecasts alone.

News Alignment contributes directly to the Confidence Score.

High uncertainty should favor patience over execution.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall evaluate current and upcoming economic news before completing any Market Thesis. The AI shall determine whether fundamental conditions support, weaken, or contradict the proposed trade and adjust the Confidence Score accordingly. When high-impact news introduces significant uncertainty, AITRAS shall recommend waiting or reassessing rather than proceeding with execution.

Contribution to Confluence Score

News Alignment should influence the overall Confidence Score as follows:

Strong Alignment: Moderate positive contribution.

Moderate Alignment: Small positive contribution.

Weak Alignment: Moderate negative contribution.

Conflicting Alignment: Significant negative contribution that may invalidate the trade until conditions stabilize.

Chapter Status

13.7 — News Alignment: Complete.

Recommendation for AITRAS

To make the News Engine more intelligent, AITRAS should classify news into operational categories before incorporating it into the Confluence Engine:

No Significant Impact – No meaningful effect expected; proceed with normal analysis.

Caution – Moderate-impact news may increase volatility; reduce confidence slightly.

Delay Execution – High-impact news is imminent; wait until the event has passed and market conditions stabilize.

Reinvestigate – News has materially changed market conditions; invalidate the current Market Thesis and perform a new analysis.

This standardized approach ensures that news is treated as a structured decision factor rather than a simple pass/fail check, making the AI's reasoning more consistent and explainable.

13.8 Risk Alignment

Evaluating Whether the Risk Profile Supports the Market Thesis

13.8.1 Definition

Risk Alignment is the process of determining whether the proposed trade complies with the project's risk management standards and whether the potential reward justifies the identified risks.

AITRAS shall evaluate risk independently of the technical setup before approving any trade.

13.8.2 Purpose

Risk Alignment helps AITRAS to:

Protect trading capital.

Ensure compliance with Risk Management rules.

Prevent overexposure.

Reject technically valid but high-risk trades.

Maintain long-term trading consistency.

13.8.3 Core Principles

Capital preservation takes priority over opportunity.

Every trade must satisfy predefined risk standards.

Risk must be proportional to confidence.

Technical quality does not override poor risk.

If risk cannot be measured accurately, the trade shall not be recommended.

13.8.4 AI Investigation Checklist

AITRAS shall determine:

Is a valid Stop Loss defined?

Is a realistic Take Profit defined?

Does the trade meet the minimum 1:3 Risk-to-Reward requirement?

Is the position size appropriate?

Is total account exposure within acceptable limits?

Are current market conditions increasing risk?

Does the overall risk profile support the Market Thesis?

13.8.5 Alignment Classification

AITRAS shall classify Risk Alignment as:

Alignment

Description

Strong Alignment

All risk requirements are satisfied and exposure is well controlled.

Moderate Alignment

Minor risk concerns exist but remain within acceptable limits.

Weak Alignment

Elevated risk reduces the quality of the trade.

Conflicting Alignment

Risk standards are violated; the trade should not proceed.

13.8.6 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Approve trades only when Risk Alignment is Strong or Moderate.

Reduce confidence for Weak Alignment.

Reject trades with Conflicting Alignment regardless of technical quality.

Explain which risk factors influenced the recommendation.

Continuously monitor risk if the trade remains active.

13.8.7 Summary

Key Principles

Risk Alignment is mandatory before execution.

Every trade must meet predefined risk standards.

Minimum Risk-to-Reward is 1:3.

Position sizing and account exposure must remain controlled.

Poor risk management overrides strong technical setups.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall independently evaluate the risk profile of every proposed trade before approval. The AI shall confirm that Stop Loss, Take Profit, position sizing, account exposure, and the minimum Risk-to-Reward requirement of 1:3 comply with the project's Risk Management framework. If any critical risk standard is violated, the trade shall be rejected regardless of technical confluence.

Contribution to Confluence Score

Risk Alignment should influence the overall Confidence Score as follows:

Strong Alignment: High positive contribution.

Moderate Alignment: Moderate positive contribution.

Weak Alignment: Moderate negative contribution.

Conflicting Alignment: Critical negative contribution resulting in automatic rejection.

Special Rule: Unlike other alignment factors, Conflicting Risk Alignment acts as a veto condition. A trade that fails the project's risk standards cannot be approved, even if all other confluence factors are favorable.

Chapter Status

13.8 — Risk Alignment: Complete.

Design Recommendation

To make AITRAS more transparent, classify the result of Risk Alignment into two outputs:

Risk Status

✅ Acceptable

⚠️ Elevated

❌ Unacceptable

AI Action

Proceed – Risk standards satisfied.

Proceed with Caution – Minor concerns; continue monitoring.

Wait – Improve trade conditions before entry.

Reject – Risk framework violated.

This separation makes it clear that technical confluence determines whether a setup is attractive, while Risk Alignment determines whether it is permissible to trade.

13.9 Confidence Score

Measuring the Strength of the Market Thesis

13.9.1 Definition

The Confidence Score is a numerical assessment of how strongly the available evidence supports the current Market Thesis.

AITRAS shall calculate this score after evaluating all confluence factors and use it to communicate the strength of its analysis, not the certainty of the market outcome.

13.9.2 Purpose

The Confidence Score helps AITRAS to:

Measure the quality of the Market Thesis.

Standardize decision-making.

Compare multiple trading opportunities.

Communicate confidence transparently.

Support consistent and objective recommendations.

13.9.3 Core Principles

The score reflects evidence, not certainty.

Higher confidence requires stronger confluence.

Contradictory evidence reduces confidence.

Confidence must be explainable.

The score must be recalculated whenever new information becomes available.

13.9.4 Evidence Considered

AITRAS shall calculate the Confidence Score using:

Trend Alignment.

Structure Alignment.

Liquidity Alignment.

Order Block Alignment.

Fair Value Gap Alignment.

Session Alignment.

News Alignment.

Risk Alignment.

Higher-Timeframe Bias.

Historical Pattern Memory.

Contradictory evidence.

13.9.5 Confidence Classification

AITRAS shall classify the Confidence Score as:

Score

Classification

Meaning

90–100

Very High

Exceptional confluence with minimal conflicting evidence.

75–89

High

Strong evidence supports the Market Thesis.

60–74

Moderate

Valid setup with some uncertainty.

40–59

Low

Weak confluence; caution required.

Below 40

Very Low

Insufficient evidence; trade should not be recommended.

These ranges measure the strength of the analysis, not the likelihood that the trade will be profitable.

13.9.6 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Calculate the Confidence Score only after all alignment checks are complete.

Reduce the score when high-priority evidence conflicts.

Explain the major factors that influenced the score.

Recalculate the score whenever the Market Thesis changes.

Never recommend a trade based solely on a high score if mandatory rules (such as Risk Management) have failed.

13.9.7 Summary

Key Principles

Confidence reflects evidence quality, not prediction accuracy.

Strong confluence produces higher confidence.

Contradictory evidence lowers confidence.

Confidence is dynamic and must be updated as markets evolve.

Risk Management rules always take precedence over the Confidence Score.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall calculate a Confidence Score only after completing the full Confluence Engine evaluation. The score shall represent the strength of the supporting evidence for the Market Thesis and shall be accompanied by an explanation of the primary factors that increased or decreased confidence. The Confidence Score shall never override mandatory risk management or validation rules.

Recommended Decision Thresholds

To standardize AITRAS' behavior, use the Confidence Score together with the validation rules:

Confidence Score

AI Recommendation

90–100

Strong Buy / Strong Sell (all validation rules satisfied)

75–89

Buy / Sell

60–74

Monitor for Confirmation

40–59

Wait

Below 40

Reject Setup

Important: These recommendations are valid only if Risk Management, Invalidation Rules, and the AI Strategy Validation Checklist have all been passed. A trade with a confidence score of 95 should still be rejected if it violates a mandatory rule, such as failing the minimum 1:3 Risk-to-Reward requirement.

Chapter Status

Chapter 13.9 — Confidence Score: Complete.

Recommendation for Future Implementation

When AITRAS is implemented, each recommendation should include a transparent explanation, for example:

Confidence Score: 87/100 (High)

Primary Strengths: Trend Alignment, Market Structure, Liquidity, Order Block.

Primary Weaknesses: Moderate news uncertainty.

Risk Status: Acceptable.

Final Recommendation: Buy.

Reasoning: "The higher-timeframe bullish trend is supported by bullish market structure, a fresh demand Order Block, and a recent liquidity sweep. Although moderate-impact news is scheduled later in the session, the overall evidence strongly supports the current Market Thesis."

This approach makes the AI's conclusions explainable, auditable, and easier for users to trust because every recommendation is backed by clearly stated evidence rather than a single number.

14.2 High-Impact Events

Identifying and Managing Major Economic Events

14.2.1 Definition

High-Impact Events are scheduled or unscheduled economic, monetary, or geopolitical events that have the potential to cause significant market volatility, rapid price movements, and changes in market sentiment.

AITRAS shall identify these events, assess their relevance, and incorporate their potential impact into all market analyses and trade recommendations.

14.2.2 Purpose

High-Impact Event analysis helps AITRAS to:

Identify periods of elevated market risk.

Anticipate increased volatility.

Protect traders from unnecessary exposure.

Improve the timing of trade execution.

Integrate fundamental events into the Market Thesis.

14.2.3 Core Principles

Not all news events have the same market impact.

High-impact events can temporarily override technical analysis.

Market reaction is often more important than market expectations.

Volatility may increase before, during, and after the event.

High-impact events require enhanced risk management.

14.2.4 Common High-Impact Events

AITRAS shall monitor major categories including:

Central Bank Events

Interest Rate Decisions.

Monetary Policy Statements.

Press Conferences.

Meeting Minutes.

Employment Data

Non-Farm Payrolls (NFP).

Unemployment Rate.

Employment Change Reports.

Average Hourly Earnings.

Inflation Data

Consumer Price Index (CPI).

Producer Price Index (PPI).

Core Inflation Measures.

Economic Growth

Gross Domestic Product (GDP).

Retail Sales.

Industrial Production.

Manufacturing and Services PMI.

Other Major Events

Speeches by central bank officials.

Emergency policy announcements.

Major geopolitical developments.

Significant financial crises or market disruptions.

14.2.5 AI Investigation Checklist

AITRAS shall determine:

Is a high-impact event scheduled?

Which currencies or markets are affected?

How much time remains before the event?

What level of volatility is expected?

Does the event support or challenge the current Market Thesis?

Should new positions be delayed?

Should existing positions be managed differently?

14.2.6 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Identify all relevant high-impact events before recommending a trade.

Increase caution as the event approaches.

Recommend delaying new entries when appropriate.

Reassess the Market Thesis immediately after the event.

Clearly explain how the event influences the analysis and risk assessment.

14.2.7 Common Mistakes

Avoid:

Treating all economic events equally.

Ignoring high-impact events because technical analysis appears strong.

Assuming forecast values will be accurate.

Entering new trades immediately before major announcements without justification.

Failing to reassess after the market reacts.

14.2.8 Summary

Key Definition

High-Impact Events are major economic or geopolitical developments capable of significantly influencing market direction, volatility, and trader sentiment.

Key Principles

Prioritize events with historically significant market impact.

Prepare before the event, not after.

Analyze the market's reaction rather than relying only on forecasts.

Incorporate high-impact events into Risk Management and the Market Thesis.

Increase caution during periods of elevated uncertainty.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall identify and evaluate all relevant high-impact events before finalizing any Market Thesis or trade recommendation. The AI shall assess their potential effect on volatility, market sentiment, and risk, adjust the Confidence Score where appropriate, and recommend delaying, modifying, or rejecting trades when the expected impact materially increases uncertainty.

Recommendation for AITRAS

Rather than treating all high-impact events equally, AITRAS should classify them by operational impact:

Event Category

Typical AI Response

Interest Rate Decisions

Highest priority; reassess all affected Market Theses.

Inflation Data (CPI/PPI)

Increase caution; expect elevated volatility.

Employment Reports (e.g., NFP)

Delay new entries until post-release conditions stabilize.

GDP and Major Growth Data

Evaluate impact on medium- and long-term market bias.

Unexpected Geopolitical Events

Trigger immediate reassessment and continuous monitoring.

This approach allows AITRAS to respond differently based on the nature of the event instead of applying a single rule to all news releases, making the News Intelligence module more realistic and adaptable.

Chapter 14 — News Intelligence

Chapter 14 — News Intelligence

14.1 Economic Calendar

Understanding Scheduled Economic Events and Their Market Impact

14.1.1 Definition

The Economic Calendar is a structured schedule of upcoming economic events, reports, and official announcements that have the potential to influence financial markets.

AITRAS shall use the Economic Calendar to anticipate periods of increased volatility, assess fundamental risk, and incorporate scheduled events into its market analysis.

14.1.2 Purpose

The Economic Calendar helps AITRAS to:

Monitor upcoming economic events.

Identify periods of expected market volatility.

Assess potential risks before trade execution.

Improve timing of market analysis and trade recommendations.

Integrate fundamental analysis with technical analysis.

14.1.3 Core Principles

Scheduled economic events can significantly influence market behavior.

The importance of an event depends on its expected market impact.

Both the scheduled event and the market's reaction should be considered.

Economic events must be reviewed before any trade recommendation.

The calendar provides context, not certainty.

14.1.4 Information to Collect

For every scheduled event, AITRAS shall record:

Event name.

Date and time.

Time zone.

Affected currency or financial instrument.

Country or economic region.

Impact level (Low, Medium, High).

Previous value.

Forecast value.

Actual value (when released).

Event status (Upcoming, Live, Completed).

14.1.5 AI Investigation Checklist

Before recommending a trade, AITRAS shall determine:

Are there any scheduled economic events affecting the traded currency pair?

How soon will the next event occur?

What is the expected impact level?

Could the event invalidate the current Market Thesis?

Should execution be delayed until after the announcement?

Has the event already occurred, and if so, how did the market react?

14.1.6 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Continuously monitor the Economic Calendar.

Highlight upcoming high-impact events in all market reports.

Recommend caution or delayed execution when significant events are imminent.

Reassess the Market Thesis after major economic releases.

Clearly explain how scheduled events influenced the analysis.

14.1.7 Common Mistakes

Avoid:

Ignoring scheduled high-impact events.

Assuming forecasts will match actual outcomes.

Trading immediately before major announcements without sufficient justification.

Treating the calendar as a prediction tool rather than a source of risk awareness.

Failing to update the analysis after the event has occurred.

14.1.8 Summary

Key Definition

The Economic Calendar is the primary source of scheduled economic events that may influence market behavior and should be reviewed before every trading decision.

Key Principles

Monitor all relevant economic events.

Focus on events affecting the traded currencies.

Consider timing and expected impact.

Evaluate both expectations and actual outcomes.

Integrate calendar information into the overall Market Thesis.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall consult the Economic Calendar before completing any market analysis or trade recommendation. The AI shall identify scheduled events affecting the relevant instruments, assess their potential impact, and incorporate this information into the Market Thesis, Risk Assessment, and Confidence Score.

Recommendation for AITRAS

I recommend that AITRAS categorize every economic event into one of four operational states:

Status

AI Action

Upcoming

Monitor and prepare for potential impact.

Imminent (e.g., within the next 30–60 minutes)

Delay new trade entries unless there is a documented exception.

Released

Analyze the actual result and the immediate market reaction.

Resolved

Incorporate the event into historical memory and continue normal analysis.

This gives the News Engine a structured workflow and ensures that scheduled economic events are treated consistently throughout the system.

14.3 Breaking News

Detecting and Responding to Unexpected Market Events

14.3.1 Definition

Breaking News refers to unexpected events or announcements that occur without prior scheduling and have the potential to significantly influence financial markets.

AITRAS shall continuously monitor reliable news sources to detect breaking events and evaluate their impact on the current Market Thesis.

14.3.2 Purpose

Breaking News analysis helps AITRAS to:

Detect unexpected market-moving events.

Respond quickly to changing market conditions.

Protect traders from sudden volatility.

Update or invalidate the Market Thesis when necessary.

Improve situational awareness during live market conditions.

14.3.3 Core Principles

Breaking News is unpredictable.

Speed is important, but accuracy is more important.

News should be verified before influencing trading decisions.

Market reaction often evolves over time.

Unexpected events can invalidate existing technical analysis.

14.3.4 Common Sources of Breaking News

AITRAS shall monitor trusted sources for:

Central bank emergency announcements.

Government policy changes.

Geopolitical developments.

Natural disasters affecting markets.

Major corporate announcements (where relevant).

Financial crises or banking events.

Unexpected economic statements.

Significant market disruptions.

14.3.5 AI Investigation Checklist

When Breaking News is detected, AITRAS shall determine:

What happened?

Which markets or currencies are affected?

Has the information been verified by reliable sources?

What is the expected level of market impact?

Does the event invalidate the current Market Thesis?

Should open positions be reassessed?

Should new trades be delayed until conditions stabilize?

14.3.6 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Detect and verify breaking news before acting.

Immediately reassess the Market Thesis if the event is significant.

Reduce the Confidence Score when uncertainty increases.

Recommend delaying or avoiding new trades during periods of extreme uncertainty.

Clearly explain how the breaking news affected the analysis.

14.3.7 Common Mistakes

Avoid:

Reacting to unverified rumors.

Assuming the first market reaction reflects the long-term impact.

Ignoring breaking news because technical signals remain favorable.

Failing to reassess open trades after significant developments.

Continuing with outdated analysis after market conditions have changed.

14.3.8 Summary

Key Definition

Breaking News consists of unexpected events that can rapidly alter market conditions and require immediate reassessment of the Market Thesis.

Key Principles

Verify information before acting.

Prioritize trusted and authoritative sources.

Reassess both open and planned trades.

Adjust the Confidence Score based on verified developments.

Allow the market time to reveal its true reaction when appropriate.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall continuously monitor for verified Breaking News that may affect the relevant markets. Upon detecting a significant event, the AI shall reassess the Market Thesis, evaluate the impact on open and planned trades, adjust the Confidence Score where necessary, and recommend delaying, modifying, or cancelling trades if market conditions have materially changed.

Recommendation for AITRAS

To make the News Intelligence module more robust, AITRAS should classify Breaking News by response priority:

Priority

Description

AI Action

Low

Limited market relevance.

Monitor and continue normal analysis.

Medium

May influence specific currencies or sectors.

Recalculate the Market Thesis and reduce confidence if necessary.

High

Significant impact on one or more major markets.

Reassess all affected analyses and consider delaying new entries.

Critical

Extraordinary event causing severe market disruption or uncertainty.

Immediately invalidate affected Market Theses, recommend suspending new trade recommendations, and initiate a full market reinvestigation.

This structured response ensures that AITRAS reacts proportionally to the severity of the event rather than treating all breaking news with the same level of urgency.

14.4 Fundamental Analysis

Evaluating Economic Conditions to Understand Market Direction

14.4.1 Definition

Fundamental Analysis is the process of evaluating economic, monetary, financial, and geopolitical factors to determine their influence on the value of a currency and the overall market direction.

AITRAS shall use Fundamental Analysis to complement technical analysis and strengthen the Market Thesis.

14.4.2 Purpose

Fundamental Analysis helps AITRAS to:

Understand the underlying drivers of market movements.

Assess the economic strength or weakness of currencies.

Confirm or challenge technical analysis.

Build medium- and long-term market bias.

Improve the accuracy of the Market Thesis.

14.4.3 Core Principles

Markets are influenced by both technical and fundamental factors.

Strong economies generally support stronger currencies.

Weak economic conditions generally weaken currencies.

Monetary policy has a significant influence on exchange rates.

Fundamentals provide context, while technical analysis provides execution.

14.4.4 Key Fundamental Factors

AITRAS shall evaluate:

Economic Growth

Gross Domestic Product (GDP).

Industrial Production.

Retail Sales.

Manufacturing and Services PMI.

Inflation

Consumer Price Index (CPI).

Producer Price Index (PPI).

Core Inflation.

Employment

Non-Farm Payrolls (NFP).

Unemployment Rate.

Wage Growth.

Employment Change.

Monetary Policy

Interest Rates.

Central Bank Decisions.

Monetary Policy Statements.

Quantitative Tightening or Easing.

Market Sentiment

Risk-On vs. Risk-Off environment.

Investor confidence.

Global capital flows.

Geopolitical Factors

Elections.

Trade policies.

Wars and geopolitical conflicts.

Government policy changes.

Major international events.

14.4.5 AI Investigation Checklist

AITRAS shall determine:

What is the current economic outlook for each currency?

Is inflation rising or falling?

What is the direction of interest rates?

Is employment improving or weakening?

What is the current central bank stance?

Are geopolitical developments influencing the market?

Do the fundamentals support or contradict the technical Market Thesis?

14.4.6 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Evaluate relevant economic data before forming a Market Thesis.

Combine fundamental and technical analysis objectively.

Explain how fundamental conditions influence the analysis.

Reduce confidence when fundamentals contradict technical evidence.

Reassess the Market Thesis whenever significant fundamental information changes.

14.4.7 Common Mistakes

Avoid:

Relying only on technical analysis.

Ignoring macroeconomic trends.

Reacting to individual data releases without considering the broader economic context.

Assuming one economic indicator determines market direction.

Treating fundamentals as a precise timing tool for entries.

14.4.8 Summary

Key Definition

Fundamental Analysis evaluates the economic and financial conditions that influence currency values and market direction, providing the broader context for technical trading decisions.

Key Principles

Analyze the overall economy, not just individual events.

Consider multiple economic indicators together.

Evaluate central bank policy and interest rates.

Monitor market sentiment and geopolitical developments.

Use fundamentals to guide market bias and technical analysis to refine execution.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall incorporate Fundamental Analysis into every Market Thesis by evaluating the relevant economic environment, monetary policy, inflation, employment, market sentiment, and geopolitical conditions. The AI shall explain how these factors support or contradict the technical analysis and adjust the Confidence Score accordingly.

Recommendation for AITRAS

Rather than treating all fundamental information equally, AITRAS should organize its analysis into four layers:

Layer

Focus

Purpose

Macroeconomic Environment

Growth, inflation, employment

Determine overall economic strength.

Monetary Policy

Interest rates and central bank stance

Assess likely currency direction.

Market Sentiment

Risk appetite, capital flows, investor behavior

Understand current market positioning.

Geopolitical Environment

Political and global events

Identify external risks and opportunities.

This layered approach enables AITRAS to reason systematically, moving from the broad economic landscape to specific market implications. It also aligns well with the project's principle of evidence before conclusions, ensuring that the AI forms its Market Thesis from multiple independent sources rather than isolated indicators.

14.5 News Memory

Learning from Historical News Events and Their Market Impact

14.5.1 Definition

News Memory is the AI's long-term repository of historical news events, their market impact, and the resulting outcomes.

AITRAS shall use this memory to compare current events with historical cases, identify recurring patterns, and improve future market analysis.

14.5.2 Purpose

News Memory helps AITRAS to:

Build historical knowledge of market reactions.

Recognize recurring economic patterns.

Improve future Market Theses.

Support confidence scoring with historical evidence.

Continuously learn from previous analyses.

14.5.3 Core Principles

Every significant news event is a learning opportunity.

Historical events provide context, not certainty.

Similar events may produce different outcomes under different market conditions.

Historical comparisons should strengthen reasoning, not replace current analysis.

News Memory should evolve continuously.

14.5.4 Information to Store

For each significant news event, AITRAS shall record:

Event name.

Event category.

Date and time.

Affected currency pair(s).

Previous, forecast, and actual values (where applicable).

Immediate market reaction.

Short-term impact.

Long-term impact.

Market Thesis before the event.

Final market outcome.

Lessons learned.

14.5.5 AI Investigation Checklist

When analyzing current news, AITRAS shall determine:

Has a similar event occurred before?

How did the market react previously?

What similarities exist?

What differences exist?

Are current market conditions comparable?

Does historical evidence support the current Market Thesis?

14.5.6 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Compare current news with historical events stored in News Memory.

Identify recurring market behavior where appropriate.

Use historical comparisons to support, not replace, current evidence.

Update News Memory after every significant event.

Explain when historical news influenced the analysis.

14.5.7 Common Mistakes

Avoid:

Assuming history will repeat exactly.

Ignoring changes in the economic environment.

Relying on historical events without considering current market conditions.

Storing incomplete or inaccurate event records.

Giving historical events greater importance than current evidence.

14.5.8 Summary

Key Definition

News Memory is AITRAS' historical database of significant economic events and their market outcomes, enabling the AI to learn from past market behavior and strengthen future analysis.

Key Principles

Record every significant news event.

Compare current events with historical cases.

Learn from outcomes and refine future analysis.

Treat historical evidence as supporting information.

Continuously update the knowledge base.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall maintain a structured News Memory containing historical economic events, market reactions, and trading outcomes. During every market analysis, the AI shall compare relevant current events with similar historical cases, identify meaningful similarities and differences, and use this information as supporting evidence when forming the Market Thesis and Confidence Score. Historical comparisons shall inform, but never override, current market evidence.

Recommendation for AITRAS

To maximize learning, organize News Memory into three levels:

Memory Level

Purpose

Event Memory

Stores the details of each individual news event and its outcome.

Pattern Memory

Identifies recurring reactions to similar types of events (e.g., repeated NFP or CPI behavior).

Strategic Memory

Records lessons learned, such as when certain news types consistently strengthened, weakened, or invalidated Market Theses under specific market conditions.

This hierarchy transforms News Memory from a simple archive into an adaptive knowledge system. Instead of merely remembering that an event occurred, AITRAS learns how similar events have behaved over time and incorporates those lessons into future analyses while still prioritizing current market conditions.

14.6 Expected Volatility

Estimating Future Market Volatility from Fundamental and Technical Evidence

14.6.1 Definition

Expected Volatility is the process of forecasting the likely level of market price movement over a future period based on scheduled news events, market conditions, historical behavior, and technical analysis.

AITRAS shall estimate expected volatility before making any trading recommendation.

14.6.2 Purpose

Expected Volatility helps AITRAS to:

Anticipate periods of increased market movement.

Improve trade timing.

Adjust Risk Management strategies.

Determine whether market conditions are suitable for trading.

Strengthen the Market Thesis with volatility expectations.

14.6.3 Core Principles

Volatility is dynamic and continuously changing.

High-impact news generally increases volatility.

Low-volatility markets often produce smaller price movements.

High volatility increases both opportunity and risk.

Volatility should influence execution, not determine market direction.

14.6.4 Factors Influencing Expected Volatility

AITRAS shall evaluate:

Economic Events

High-impact scheduled news.

Central bank announcements.

Employment reports.

Inflation releases.

GDP reports.

Breaking News

Geopolitical developments.

Emergency government announcements.

Financial crises.

Unexpected economic events.

Market Conditions

Current market sentiment.

Existing trend strength.

Recent volatility.

Liquidity conditions.

Historical Behaviour

Previous reactions to similar events.

Typical volatility during comparable market conditions.

Session-specific volatility patterns.

Technical Factors

Current market structure.

Liquidity concentration.

Fair Value Gaps.

Price compression or expansion.

Range size.

14.6.5 AI Investigation Checklist

AITRAS shall determine:

Are major news events approaching?

What level of volatility is expected?

Which currencies are most likely to be affected?

Does expected volatility support or weaken the current strategy?

Should position size be adjusted?

Should execution be delayed?

Does expected volatility change the Risk Assessment?

14.6.6 Volatility Classification

AITRAS shall classify Expected Volatility as:

Level

Description

AI Response

Very Low

Quiet market with limited movement expected.

Trade selectively and avoid unrealistic profit targets.

Low

Stable market conditions with moderate opportunity.

Normal strategy execution.

Moderate

Healthy trading environment with balanced movement.

Preferred trading conditions.

High

Strong price movement expected.

Increase caution, review Stop Loss and position sizing.

Extreme

Exceptional volatility with unpredictable movement.

Delay execution or trade only under exceptional confluence.

14.6.7 AI Decision Rules

AITRAS shall:

Estimate Expected Volatility before every Market Thesis.

Adjust the Confidence Score based on anticipated market conditions.

Recommend appropriate Risk Management adjustments.

Warn when expected volatility exceeds acceptable trading conditions.

Recalculate the assessment whenever new information becomes available.

14.6.8 Common Mistakes

Avoid:

Assuming high volatility always creates better opportunities.

Ignoring volatility when setting Stop Loss or Take Profit levels.

Confusing market direction with market volatility.

Relying solely on historical volatility without considering current events.

Failing to reassess volatility after major news releases.

14.6.9 Summary

Key Definition

Expected Volatility is the AI's estimate of future market movement based on fundamental events, historical behavior, technical conditions, and current market sentiment.

Key Principles

Volatility measures movement, not direction.

Forecast volatility before entering any trade.

Combine fundamental and technical evidence.

Adapt risk management to expected market conditions.

Continuously update volatility expectations as new information becomes available.

AI Rule

AITRAS shall estimate Expected Volatility before completing any Market Thesis or trade recommendation. The AI shall evaluate scheduled economic events, breaking news, historical market behavior, technical conditions, and current sentiment to forecast future market activity. The resulting volatility assessment shall influence Risk Management, trade execution timing, and the overall Confidence Score, but shall not independently determine market direction.

Recommendation for AITRAS

Expected Volatility should directly influence the AI's execution strategy rather than simply acting as informational data.

Expected Volatility

AI Execution Behaviour

Very Low

Trade only the highest-quality setups, expecting limited price movement.

Low

Apply the standard strategy with conservative expectations.

Moderate

Normal execution; this is the preferred environment for most setups.

High

Tighten trade selection, reduce position size if necessary, and confirm strong confluence before entry.

Extreme

Suspend new trade recommendations unless exceptional confluence and risk conditions are satisfied.
